And so pierce the conjunctiva only, not too deeply but lightly within; then fill it with honey paste as we have said; and at the completion of this work, prepare the bedding for the patient to sleep on his back in a dimly lit place; ensure all movement is gentle, provide him light foods, do not move his head nor turn left or right, bind according to its natural position until the third day; then remove from that dark room and inspect his eye, show him things occasionally, and reconnect the ligament until the seventh day. It should not be done in the hour of cure or after incision now but rather when it is needed because the water rises rapidly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 If an abscess comes about, you should drain the oil before the seventh day, and apply to what soothes the abscess; and when it is calmed, uncover the eye-sockets and keep covered with a cloth for several days, staying in that darkened room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 Gradually leave the house and venture outside more frequently, and it will improve in its own way; and know that no pupils should intervene in this matter.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	It is not known to our lands nor can be found in our books; and never it does such things.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are forms similar to elephantiasis, because those who do not know them mistake their appearance; and they are properly of the rain.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And these include a subtlety in its head, with three sharp corners on it.
de la char sor le neis	Of the cartilage from under the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Sometimes oranges and other pus-filled growths appear, some of which resemble many scorpions in size; and if there are such growths with hairs colored by blood, and they have skin that is lighter than normal.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 In that case for these chests which are hollow and not infected, it is necessary to make the patient sit between your hands towards the sun; and work on its nostrils, and pour molten wax into those cavities, and then draw out the hairs; hence remove what you hold with a spatula of fine subtlety from one side, as long as you know that such chest is completely bone.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If there is anything left that cannot be covered, work over all the subtle veins lightly, ensuring nothing remains; and if they become inflamed or an abscess forms, treat as it should; and if malignant abscesses occur, quickly cauterize until the area becomes firm and the bones are laid bare, then pour oil, milk, water, or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If he does not work, and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is safe; and if moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is a hole in the bone above, through which drainage cannot pass: then it is necessary for you to tie a linen thread slightly thickened, and soak it with your hands, leaving space between each one of us; place the patient's head on the end of the filament as far as possible, and draw gently until it comes out through the nostrcuil inside the mouth; many times they do this for school children, and it is an easy thing for those who know how to do it; then hold the upper part that comes from the nose in one hand, and the lower part coming from the mouth in the other hand, and determine each one after us as if we were a filament.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Do as long as you know that the nerves have been corrupted in that vessel, then draw out the blood, wipe off the vein with an Egyptian salve, and place it back properly near the eyes as before; do this for III days or more until the ointment dissolves all that is retained from the vessel; and then place a plaster of aloes on it without delay until healed, and if there is need for dry medicines, use them; and this is the method of using the instrument to purge the head, which allows distillation of oils and other medicine near the eyes.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	Et le sire du mout se vous doit si lesme:
de la char sor le neis	Of the cartilage from under the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there arises at the top of the neck a disease called "telul," which grows and becomes large until it is visible to the eye; therefore, it must be excised from the beginning, with the bone cut out completely, then place the caustic or burning medicine on it. And if one delays in cutting before it becomes large, observe if it is hard, of a strange color, and has poor sensation: do not touch it with iron as it is an infected abscess that worsens each time; when it is cut once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is from soft tissue, without strange coloring, and you can see all of it can be covered, then take away the fear in the patient, cure the area with dry and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the neck is cut and closed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when a solution for continued treatment enters one of these cartilaginous wounds, it is beneficial in few cases and even to some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Thus, when this occurs in anyone, look to see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; then sew up the two sides, and treat until it heals; and if the edges are torn apart on both sides, make sure you scrape off all parts of their core until they heal, then join the two sides together with a suture, reinforce, and apply powdered dragon's blood consecutively; and put over the powders a piece of alabaster strong or other alabaster, and leave it to ooze through itself, then treat with salve until healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way to sew is that you assemble the stitches: with needles, as we have said in suturing the abd <stomach>; or with thread, as I have instructed you before.
des apostemes des levres	For abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	On the hand's surface, hard pus-filled abscesses appear like grains of wheat, both smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips, cut above each one, take it with tweezebrushes and apply to each part; then place the ointment after vitriol incisions so that the wound is cleansed; and finally, ease the pain, and treat the area dry until healed.
de la char des gencives	From teeth decay
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Lei.
des sordens	Of strains
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Of strains are never gathered at the heads of teeth, deep in the mouth between the gums, which are unpleasant and rough scales; nor are they ever black or citrine or worms until corruption comes to the gum, and they become foul breathing. It is necessary that you make the patient sit with his head between your hands, and his teeth in your holy hand, and remove any teeth or scales found, as long as nothing remains; then do so with darkness and greenness, and yellowness and other pains until they are removed; and if something has been taken out due to the first reason, it is good; if not, resume on the second day and afterward, until you have everything extracted. Be aware that teeth require various forms of estrangement for relief according to what the work shows, because the razors from which teeth fail are different in form than those between them. These shapes and others must be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat teeth pain to delay the drawing out as long as possible, because it should not be done hastily; for this matter has great difficulty until there is no excuse to extract.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then when the patient is strained by tearing, you must ensure certainty of toothache.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Many times the pain torments the patient, and he thinks it is a tooth causing it, and makes him extract the bad tooth; however, the pain does not go away for this reason alone, as long as the evil spirit persists, which we have already addressed with these saints; and when you are well convinced of the tooth aching, it must be that you scrape around the tooth with a strong spatula to protect the gum from all sides; then move it with your fingers or fine pliers little by little until it is properly aligned, then securely fix the pliers; and let the head of the shoulder rest in its place between your knuckles, so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After an extraction of the tooth, break it off completely; and if it does not fall out on its own, take one of these extractors and insert them gently into each side, and move it as you did initially.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is pierced and knocked out, you must fill it with gauze where the roots are; and gently use forceps for extraction so that it does not break during removal; and work diligently around the gums to preserve the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And be careful not to break it and leave a part of the root; and let this cause greater pain for the patient due to the remaining root's evilness.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And be careful not to act as ignorant surgeons do, who hastily and recklessly break the cartilage every time, and fail to apply what we have mentioned; but they often bring about great disease from the roots that remain or from the broken cartilage, as we have often seen. When a tooth is extracted, wash it thoroughly with wine or herbs and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, then fill the cavity with powdered alum; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the tendons to which one moves first have long points and large thicknesses, not double when you pull on the thread; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be large limbs such that they do not bend while pulling, and made of well-crafted iron with teeth to grip hold.
de la racine des dens	from the root of tendons
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains at the tear, you must place a piece of cotton soaked in butter on it for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 As long as the eyes are softened, then apply the pincers called "algèfre," which make the head appear like a sparrow's beak; and inside they should be made just like a file.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not come out with all these pincers, it is necessary to uncover the entire flesh around the root and use the instrument called "althali," which is a pair of forceps. This is how it looks like.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is thick and large enough so that it does not break, and the root slips through this, then it's good. If not, use all instruments, as these forms come here afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you help with this instrument that has two tines, then it is like the form shown here:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And of other instruments to be used on teeth, and this device which appears as large pincers, here is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And these instruments must be forged so that they cannot break; and there are many tooth instruments; likewise other instruments which are not counted as such. The wise masters skillfully discover by themselves their instrument according to the works and diseases shown to them, for some illnesses do not have a specific instrument taught by old masters due to the diversity of areas and bones that may break or deteriorate; so it seeks those instruments which are needed as I mentioned before, along with guiding gestures, here is their form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-fitting to hold the bone without slipping but able to grip and extract; then restore it with medicines suitable for that, and if there is deterioration in the bones, and it is small, he has all this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When teeth appear not in their natural place within the body and are unsightly, especially in maidens, it is necessary to ascertain whether the roots of the teeth are above or below the bone, and if they are not where they should be, and cannot be filed down or smoothed: then scrape them; and if accompanied by a cyst with the tooth, take this instrument whose shape is shown here, similar to a small beak, made of iron with an acute point at one end.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And gently and gradually bend the tooth over several days due to its hardness, and because you should not move the others, and if it is possible to see that it can be filed, then grind with an instrument shaped as shown here.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the grinding of needles; and gently file the tooth over time until it comes loose; then smooth it out completely with a rasp at the end, and if the root is too sharp and cuts the tongue, it is necessary to grind the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the teeth are loose from either tapping or falling out, and the patient cannot press them together to stop them from moving without letting saliva escape despite being treated with medicines that constrict but do not work; then they should be bound with a gold wire, for silver wire becomes greenish and corrocks, but gold never changes. The wire should be of medium thickness according to the space between the teeth; if you see them tilting towards each other, take the wire and wrap it twice around two healthy teeth on either side, then place the heads of the loose teeth in-between until there are one or more left, continue this process carefully until they touch a healthy tooth on the opposite side. Then cover again up to where you started and gently and skillfully pull outwards; stop as soon as it moves no further. Hold firmly at the root of the loose tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then clamp the head of the bone with pliers, and assemble them, positioning between a healthy tooth, ensuring it does not touch the tongue; then leave it as tight as it can remain, and if it dislocates or the wires shift, restrain with another wire; if left in place, it will serve for its entire duration, forming the shape of two teeth and the figure of their immediate healthy neighboring teeth:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, if you put it back in its place freshly as we have said; and do not attempt this with anyone who is not skilled and patient, and never shape it like a dog's bone, but place it where it was missing, and restrain it as previously mentioned, and it serves for long periods of time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	Of the cautery of the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Never is this kind of wire that comes from under the tongue or nature, to be placed as such; and by accident in a recently sealed wound; and the procedures are as follows when working on the mouth of the patient, enserve their head intact, lift the tongue; then clamp the nerve ligament wide, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or swelling, it's a sign of a fresh wound, so insert the needle and clamp that part; ensure the fissure is not too deep for the artery underneath; and once done, raise a cloth of rosewater and warm water, then place it under the tongue; each night apply a linen bandage to let the eye rest.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 If blood flow is affected, put vitriol paste on the wound; if it does not stop bleeding, use the slow-burning cauterization method, which is good for this, then treat with another remedy until healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that it is colored or black or hardened, so the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, because this is cancer; and if it recedes toward a blister, and there is moisture, apply liniment generously, then extract with a delicate syringe; and remove from all sides. And if it has been healed at your treatment site, apply vitriol paste until dry, then return to the original work until you have finished everything; then raise the head on pillows of rose water and cold water, and continue with other treatments until well-healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Never does a goitre come to the throat called "godath", and they are properly known as two nuts, so when you treat them according to what we've described in division, if not healed, be cautious: if it is an abscess of little sensitivity and soft color, do not touch with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch with iron, also for bleeding; leave it until it heals completely, then you may divide it, as it might break on its own; and if it has a pale color and thin roots, have an instrument prepared to cut, but first ensure that the abscess rests and is calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Once, make the patient sit in front of the sun, and their head is in your hand, and work the mouth and press the instrument with the servants between your hands, pressing the tongue from all sides; and be made of silver or fine iron as a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue against this instrument entirely so that you see the abscess and take its edge with your fingernail to insert it into one almond, and draw as much blood above what you can; then do not touch anything else. Then cover the instrument (with something), which has the form shown here: (the translation for this part ends)
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument with tongs, use a spatula of which here is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And take the incision with a sharp tool from one side and another name; and when you have cut out one of the almonds, do so on the other in the same manner, then after the incision rinse the patient's throat with hot water, vinegar, saltwater, and if blood flow occurs, again rinse with warm water or boiled pomegranate peels, or mistletoe leaves; continue until bleeding stops. Then treat them until they are healed; and ensure no other abscesses form in the throat except for the two almonds, which should be dealt with as such.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treated a woman for an abscess within the throat, which was small; and had carefully sealed all of her throat so that she could not breathe through the passage blocked, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained this way for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so swollen that it had spread up to be inserted through two openings of the small neck.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 I immediately performed the procedure and inserted an onocinum in one nostril, then turned it forth and pulled out a large portion of wool; then placed another piece in the other nostril without touching the edge or pressing the tongue; afterwards, I inserted the onocinum into these abscesses, took part of them, and only a small amount of blood was drawn forth; thus, the pathway of the woman's throat was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, continuously cutting out this abscess over long periods; the abscesses would recur again, filling up the space I had emptied until they became very large; then I deceived it and cauterized inside her throat: thus, it ceased growing. Then I removed these parts, and only God could do anything further after me.
de l’uve	Of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When resetting the eye, and it is empty and elongated, then be called "perpendicular"; and if it is without large size and round, then be called "eye.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is cured as we have said in the section, and the remedy does not take effect, and you see that the abscess wound heals slowly and subtly, then one must excise it; and if it is round but not long, then incise the vein. If it is blood-red or yellow or black, then make an incision into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 Because there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it as described regarding its size and length, seat the patient in front of the sun, press their tongue with the instrument mentioned earlier; then insert the needle into the eye, push downward, and follow the incision as I have detailed for two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And it is necessary that you do not cover at all the excess which goes beyond natural boundaries; for if you cover more, it causes harm to speech and voice; after incision, follow what we have said in the incision of two almonds, and treat until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient has fear of covering, then you must employ a method for calming their fears during the procedure.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 The manner of cautery is to treat an acute fever.

Li salve de le renie ceste li a lue ne puet euste li ou tu les ceutem qui ceu en la chastre le cotte à cottirent maintant, et li moust que ce tu ce li vus.ieme et l’arestem entor de ce que est sem. de la sansue de la gorge	And for obstructions in the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 Never is medicine without suction, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not benefit, then look into the throat of the patient towards the sun, then squeeze the tongue with the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see suction, tie it at one end with a small acorn or fine pincers that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if it is not suitable, then take a sponge made of wool, and place it in the patient's throat, then make hot compressions with the heated iron rod frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And if the patient experiences water issues all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 Then take a full jar of cold water and work the mouth, and let it flow enough for swallowing, and move it often in their hand; and if soon after suction feels like water, leakage occurs.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 If it does not come out as we have said, then subtly infuse the patient with vinegar using the instrument I mentioned in the smoke treatment of the eye; do this many times, for it will eventually clear up without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 The manner of the fumigation is that you gather some charcoal into a vessel covered with cloth pierced in the middle, and place the patient's head at one end; then pour your fumigant, and have the patient put their cheek against it so that the smoke does not escape but rises to its nostr [turbans] instead; and thereafter, it will clear up immediately. If it doesn't come out right away, repeat the fumigation multiple times; meanwhile, let the patient suffer thirst, eat salted and rotten things, and avoid drinking water; eventually, they must be brought to a healer through this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	The form of the instrument used to treat the sinus looks like pincers bent for insertion into the throat; it resembles a surgeon's spoon, and has roughness from limestone so that whatever is inserted cannot be removed. This is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The form of the instrument used to treat the sinuses looks like pincers for removal as this.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 There are many types of abscesses as our memory brings forth from this book and the other, they differ in perforation and cutting; and there are two ways to handle it, one is just like its appearance itself, and because of moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second way is for lumps that are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 for the abscess of the head is different from those in the foundation, and the boil on the thighs is different from those that occur in joints, each has its own judgment in practice.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And if there are abscessangs that one should not pierce until they burst according to their fulfillment; and those that must be pierced when ripe, which do not burst according to their fulfillment, like an abscess near a joint.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 When abscesses occur near joints and are left until they ripen, sometimes the ligament and nerve of the joint may become corrupted, causing contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 If the abscess is near the main limb and you delay the perforation until it has ripened, it will harm the main limb; if it is near the base, pierce it only when it is ripe; one must only pierce an abscess once digestion is complete, except for those near the base which should not become overly large but remain contained and form a fistula.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	Insolé; et semblant meurt les oirent li ajoindre est l'aposteme qui apelan les autres et cestement doumesme apotmecs leaument, et asainte la percernec andre. 9n eur.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In cases where they burst, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 When an abscess is formed in place, it must be moved so that the puncture remains until digestion is complete, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce it too early, the poison of death spreads through his body, and he is filled with much filth; and sometimes the lips harden and the deepest parts become so.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if in any abscess that are pierced according to the width of the body, as the member requires it.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And it is necessary to treat small abscesses with small punctures, and large abscessamoins with large punctures, and many openings according to the size of the abscess; if in such abscesses where it is appropriate to reach the core, cover them and close up: when they become as soft as linen, and fall apart, do as you would for blisters. And for those that are split into three angles, and those punctured like a reed pipe, like ankle abscesses; and for those where you make one circular incision, and other cuts and shapes of punctures.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 For those with superficial abscesses like boils, it is necessary that you pierce them easily; and if the boil is large and has a great swelling, puncture part of the swelling at first; then leave the boil untouched until the next day, then avoid puncturing anything further; do this repeatedly over time, gradually increasing the amount each time, until the swelling disappears entirely; especially if the patient is weak in strength, or women who are pregnant, small children, or elderly individuals.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the spindle jumps at times with the swelling's bursting forth; if by chance it kills the patient, do not be dismayed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Clean this treatment with great caution, and when you have detected the abscess, open the wound, and examine if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a complete one, prepare gauze from linen or old cotton; and if they are large boils, and there are many hairs, ensure that in each you insert a tent so that they touch each other; and if you have cut around part of the skin on the abscess, and wrapped it outside, then fill it with old cotton or linen thread without moisture, up to three days; then bind it, and apply ointment until healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs in your work, treat with cold and soothing water, and apply soft bandages many times over the affected area.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if bleeding persists, treat it properly and heal, using the powders mentioned in this book. If it is winter or spring when an abscess occurs, causing great pain, place warm linen soaked in wine and oil over it; if during summer, use moistened linen with water and oil, or cold wine and oil until the third day as we have said, then drain the abscess, apply a compress, and continue treatment as necessary until healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre. des soros	Of boils.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. des scrophules	Of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 If it is necessary to reach the root and remove the core, then sew as we have said.

de squinance	If you clean them, then apply anointment as soon after treatment done; ightly.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote of the treatment for throat swelling; however, I have never seen such a practice in our land, and this is according to their writings.

For those with swollen throats, it is necessary to remove the fissure in the throat known as "epiglute;" and this is not done by doing so because all veins and the main cause of severe heat in the mouth, or in the throat, or in two almonds.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the main artery, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the impending danger from choking.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 Then indeed, when we wish to split the epiglottis, we should make incisions from above three circles or four along one small cut across, between the two circles or by the amount of the incision at the throat; and those levers are suitable for cutting through the epiglottis without any hindrance, and the blades remain long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And if the master is apprehensive, it should be extended with a cow's hide along the entire neck, then split the skin as far as the chin reaches; and avoid blood vessels, unless you see something, and then incise the sack of blood, as we have said; and demonstrated by the section of the windpipe that slips through the gap where it is torn apart, and due to loss of voice; leave the open wound exposed for a time.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time of doubt about strangulation has passed, bring together the two lips of the wound at its base, and stitch the entire edge close to the underlying cartilage; then apply medicines that promote healing until it is sound.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then take the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and they breathe through the wound, thus preventing death; and so it is commanded to leave the open wound until the illness has passed, which takes three or four days, and then they command to sew the wound and heal it, until it is cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 I saw that a maiden took hold of the knife and cut into her throat near the windpipe, and I was called to heal her, but she found as if dead.

Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hurried and sewed the wound, healing it until she was healthy again, and to the maiden there happened only that her voice turned red, and she returned after recovery; so I say in treating the epiglottis, there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	Of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien. des nous	From us

Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these abscesses come in the penis, and there is an unsightly appearance of a wart; some are malignant and others not so; it is necessary that you pluck them with a small sharp needle, and scrape and clean all thoroughly, then apply cotton ball moistened with fine Egyptian ointment; cure the area with this delicate ointment until it heals.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the abscess is malignant, of foul color and draining, one must perform a cauterization there.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. de la circoncision	Of circumcision.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not necessarily a disruption of continuity like other wounds; nonethebo-thee, when we perform this work by our own will and properly in children, it is necessary that we make the best and easiest work for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say the ancients did not mention child circumcision, for they do not use it in their laws either, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have sought the greatest part of masters and sages who performed circumcision before a day, and in their strength, and at any new moon; it was customary because there were two veils, and sometimes they would cover one with another below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Then it is regained and the pain doubles, and with the healing that may not be certain do not poke at the limb; and during the trimming of the nail, sometimes the metal escapes, causing swelling in the wound, and many times this occurs without needing further care.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the healing done using force at every fiber of the ligament, I have found the benefit of experimentation, as the forces cut just as well above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When you press your hand, make it equal in all parts; but the child must be awake around the skin; and set the manner for the first operation so that you instruct the child if they understand, only to tie the thread around the rod just enough, then allow them to breathe in all ways as possible; then let the head remain upright between your hands, rising again with no movements seen or felt by the child; then place your hand on the rod and blow or kiss it, raising it until the head of the rod is out; then cleanse well from any filth that has gathered there, then bind its head with a double thread, then tie below the point to another knot; and hold it at two points by the second tied string at the pouchet and index finger, tying between the two strings, then gently pull upward and raise the top of the rod's head; then let some blood drip slowly as it is a milder process, and put powder on and over the wound with glue from half an egg cooked unseasonably in rose water dissolved in oil of good quality and fresh, leaving it until the next day, curing again and again until healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the strength for cleansing is this: both heads are held and sharpened, and they should be as large as a hazel alike.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the inflammeblie if it is when the core inside escapes through the incision; therefore, it must be extended to your fingernail, so that the wound forms an opening; and cover equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then use pliers first, and afterwards bandage.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If it passes for three days, and the part underneath the rod is swollen, let it be until the opening has eased; gently scrape it off; bandage as you move, and guard against the area of the rod, which will not harm it at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore heal the sudden wound with powders, as we have said or discussed in treatments for powders; if it is bandaged too much and goes above, it will not harm; heal as we have said until it is clean.
dou retenement de l’urine	Holding back of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The retention of urine is due to stone formation, or frozen blood, or bowel obstruction, or similar things that we have discussed in the division; and if the urine does not flow, and you see there is a blockage by a stone located at the ureter opening or bladder neck, then it is appropriate for the patient to be positioned supine with knees bent; their feet should be placed on the back, extending the abdomen towards the upper back part, and restrain them sideways as much as possible; thus the pressure is applied to the urethra opening causing urine release. And if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you should provide extraction using an instrument called a "catheter," which has this form: made of fine silver wire, similar in thickness to bird feathers; with a length of about half a palm.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 The manner of the discharge of urine is such that you take a double thread and tie it at one end with a piece of wool or cotton, then insert the head through the wire; remove excess wool until it reaches the top of the tube, then grease the tube with oil or butter and balm of rue, and make the patient sit on a stool, and rub oil along the penis and testicle, both moistened with olive oil and water at will; then gently insert the wire into the penis until it reaches the base of the penis, then wrap the penis above towards the sheath; then insert the wire before reaching the blad지스트, and allow the patient to feel a flow as the tube approaches the emptying point, which may not be done in this order due to twisting along its path; then pull out all the wool gradually, allowing urine to follow, then remove it entirely, and collect the urine; repeat with the catheter until the bladder is emptied, and rest the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	Of bladder diseases
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When leeches or when blood comes into the bladder, and it accumulates there, and you drain with waters and medicine, and called "catheter," and is known as the instrument:

de la piere	Of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already explained the ways of stone extraction and medicines together; and we said the difference between the stones before rain, and all signs, and in which stone one must work by cutting; and with bladder, and with penis; and I will tell you plainly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which forms in the bladroids is more common in children, and it's a sign that the water leaps from the bladder resembling water in its subtlety; and there are many sand particles, and the patient feels graininess on their penis, and they urinate frequently, then become weakened; and most of these leaks affect foundations; and it is easier to treat children until they reach .iiij. (4) years old, and it's very severe in older men, and moderate for those who are between youth and age; and the cure is more straightforward for those with large stones than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 When we come to treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema, in order to expel all filth from within the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it does not hinder one's ability to urinate at any time for stones.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet and stand them up straight, so that the stone descends to the front of the blad cuisines, as you squeeze downward; then make them sit between your hands properly positioned, with their hands above their thighs, ensuring that the bladder is completely inclined backward; then aim and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, hasten to cut it there.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 If it does not come out with gentle pressure, grease your index finger of the left hand, if the patient is young or middle-aged, or use your thumb for older patients; place it in its foundation and press into the bladder stone, then when you feel movement at your finger, massage above the bladder neck; next squeeze near your finger, then guide the expelled stone to where you wish to dispose of it.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the assistant to press the bladder with their hand, and tell them to extend the cords upward with their right hand, and remove the skin that is below the cords on the part where you make an incision; then they apply a spatulum-like object for this purpose:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And do not move the stone between the joints and foundation, but to its side near the left ribcage; then position your right hand over the stone, and align your fingers with either the base or foundation, and stretch it across as wide as necessary for defecation, ensuring it is neither too large nor too narrow depending on the size of the stone. Occasionally press where your finger meets the base, so that it may pass without effort; also know if there are stones within angles or margins, which can be easily expelled. If they resemble a pod, round and smooth with easy passage for excretion.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 In cases where there are corners and edges, make the incision larger; if it does not yield, you must widen it with tweezers similar to a file tip for removing the splinter so that it doesn't escape; or you strike from above using a subtle instrument curved at the top; and if you cannot manage this way, enlarge the hole slightly, and if the skin is damaged, strain with vitriol; and if there are multiple fragments, first remove the largest at the bladder collar, then along the side, then the long piece, and any smaller ones afterward.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is quite large, you must split it further, making a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 Certain things happen to the patient: either they die or urine flows in as their eyes cannot unite again; however, always strive with the squeezing of tears and grinding with pincers until you do so by pieces; and once you have completed your work, apply incense, aloe, and dragon's blood to the wound, along with compresses, placing a cloth moistened in oil and vinegar or rose water and cold water nearby to cool any inflammeball.
