des dislocations de la hainche	Of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Joints of the thigh and shoulder only dislocate, not like other joints; the thigh joint is dislocated in four parts: inside and outside, front and back, more dislocated internally than externally, less so in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the knowledge of its dislocation is such that when joining the injured leg with the healthy one, it becomes longer and more open than the healthy joints, and the patient cannot double his knee at fire; and there are swollen legs near an abscess hot, because the hip of the thigh comes close.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of those it comes upon late is such that these accidents are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of those who experience this condition is that they keep their leg according to completion; however, do not double bend the knee in pain, and if one wishes to make them walk, but they cannot before, and holds urine, and swells with grief, and as it walks, passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of those whom it happens behind are that they cannot spread their buttocks nor double them, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the swelling is softened, and the shoulder head from the hip to below the ribs is dislocated.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The resets of this kind of dislocation are that you should reset the dislocation as soon as possible, and it remains according to its positioning, if there is no treatment; and one must not act with presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those where the dislocation is fresh and there are .iiij. ways of dislocation, hasten to return the joint, and stretch it out and draw it back, and move it right and left; perhaps it will come back on its own without needing further treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return in this way, you must send a strong minister and keep the leg tightly bound with two ropes or one band that wraps around the knee; another group of ministers extend their hands over him in such a manner as to place their hands below his elbangs, then they grip firmly with a light cord above the thigh; others touch the head at the bandage. And all extend up and down together once until the patient is lifted off the ground once and hangs suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four resemblances; and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 If not so, then attend to its resemblance when the dislocation is in the jaw, it must be supported under the ribcage, then place the band on the hip root, and the position that was away from the arm, then extend the band towards the arm, and towards the thigh; then engage other assistants with his arms, and embrace the large area of the affected hip, and extend it forward properly: it will return to its position now; and this method of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 And if you cannot hold it in this manner that we have described, it is necessary to bind the II feet of the afflicted together with a strong band above the II ankles and genitals, and let the affected leg be extended II degrees more than the other; then hang from the head of a pole, and let it rest two arms' length off the ground; then command another assistant to embrace the chest area, while others are also hanging with the afflicted person, who firmly grasps the hip region, as the joints return quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 And when the dislocation is on the underside, place the tissues, as we have said in those with gilbociousness, and properly strain the limb; then put in pegs at the head and other joints, then insert a wedge between the buttocks towards the malady below the shape; and cover it with moistened wraps around, so that the malady does not move, then extend each minister towards him, and the mire places equally to his hand the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns, it is well done.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, place on a stool and press as we have said in cases of gilbociousnss, and lay the patient with maladies onto their backs.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	When dislocations are present, it is necessary to hasten in stretching the affected leg as previously stated; place your hands on their pain above the injured area, then press with the other hand and extend towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 If the dislocation is at the fore part, it should not be stretched out or lifted off the ground but rather positioned as if the limb was originally displaced in that direction as we have said during lying on two pillows; and placed against his face, with the ligament extended as we have mentioned beforehand, and a compress applied to the joint above. When the patient extends his legs, they will become even; then place cushions between the buttocks, apply the thermometer, and use an elastic bandage so that the limb does not move; and he rests for three or four days before removing it; reapply the compress, and leave it on while walking gently until the limb is restored.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the knee joint
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The joint is dislocated in three ways: it's due to the inside and outside forces, and from behind; not from the front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at the hip, and if it does not reach the hip, know that it is dislocated; and in its restoration, all of which is for you to have the patient sit upright, extend his leg as much as he can, and place his back against his face, and put his foot under your feet; then take hold of his thigh with your hands, pull between your thumbs, then bend both sides of the hock gently; other assistants stretch his foot until the knee joint returns to its place, and the sign is that it should be slightly bent at the hip; apply a plaster over it, and bandage the leg to the thigh, tying them together strongly for III or IV days, then release. And do not let the patient move about during this time, until the limb has been made whole again.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not at all, then strengthen it greatly as we have said in the treatment of the elbow, until it becomes healthy.
de la dislocation dou talon	On ankle dislocations:
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is never fully closed or opened, but sometimes within and sometimes outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the signs are such that the ankle is swollen, and try to reach towards the part where it has dislocated: the reductions should be gentle, and you must extend lightly with your hands when touched solely.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is completely dislocated, it is necessary to make the patient sit upright directly, and you must grasp outward from the leg by the ankle above; then take your foot in one hand, then pass it twice to your right hand, and then extend upwards, and gently place the foot on top. Do this twice as we have said, moving and pulling the foot; if it returns, that's good; if not, resume the procedure, for it will return; and if it cannot be returned in such a manner, make the patient lie supine with their back against the ground, and firmly insert your heel between his thighs, and wrap bandages around so as not to shift the body. Then grasp the thigh and have other helpers extend the foot towards their hands or belt that is attached below the knee; then evenly extend each helper's force, with stirrups remaining between the thighs of the patient to retain them while being extended; then place mirrors symmetrically at its dislocation so they can be seen from both sides. Another helper inserts the healthy leg above and another grasps it below, causing the dislocated joint to return promptly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it reaches this point, apply the dressing and plug with wool on top, properly strain the foot to the leg, and watch over the nerves that are behind the ankle, ensuring that the ties are not too tight; then leave for two or three days, if the ties soften, release the strain; then remove after the third day or a quarter of it, and prevent the patient from walking for four days; and if they go beyond this period, there is no assurance that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess occurs, then it is necessary to pacify it as we have said elsewhere, until it becomes healthy.
des dois	Of the shoulders
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated, they must be extended easily with little effort.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the dislocation is in any joint of the lower back or leg, you must have the patient sit with their foot flat on the ground or a table directly under it, and place your foot against these joints firmly until they return; when they are even again, and there is nothing amiss, put a table of two fingers thick under the sole of the foot, strain firmly, leave for three days, then release; then let them rest until they are healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound comes with dislocation, and you see it needs to be restored, often the patient dies: do not presume in its treatment if you are not wise in the art and have not practiced it for long, nor if you are not compassionate and merciful or slow; be not rash. Begin with soothing treatments for abscesses hot, and leave the sick person to God's hand if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, reset the limb in place as soon as possible, lest sores grow there; and once the limb is in place, administer calming remedries for abscesses hot, and treat the wound as it should be, with dry ointments. If dislocation leads to fractures and small bones are broken or crushed, follow what we have said regarding simple illnesses; and guard against taking a path of fear, as I have advised, for this brings consequences according to your Creator, and because of the health of your armament and body.
Amen	 Amen
